Objection and Answer: Was Iblis an Angel?
The author refutes the claim that Iblis was an angel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that Iblis was not an angel but from the jinn, and the Quranic basis for this position.

Core Idea
The Quran's exception of Iblis from the angels shows he was a jinn, not an angel.

This lesson examines a key theological debate: whether Iblis was an angel who rebelled or a jinn who disobeyed. The objector points to Quranic verses where Iblis is commanded alongside the angels and excepted from their prostration, suggesting he was an angel. The author refutes this by clarifying that Iblis was from the jinn and his inclusion with the angels was by predominance (taghlib). We'll work through the objection, the answer, and a refutation of an alternative interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector cites two Quranic verses to argue that Iblis was an angel. Read them carefully.
Notice the use of 'except Iblis' as evidence.
2
Understand the answer
The author denies the premise and states Iblis was from the jinn, included among angels by predominance. Grasp the concept of taghlib.
3
Refute an alternative interpretation
Some might claim Iblis was a type of angel called 'jinn'. See how the author dismisses this as contrary to the apparent meaning.
This strengthens the main argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما منعك ألا تسجد إذ أمرتك) (1) . (۲) وبدليل صحة استثنائه منهم في قوله تعالى : فسجدوا إلا إبليس )) وقوله تعالى : ( فسجد الملائكة كلهم أجمعون إلا إبليس أبي أن يكون مع الساجدين ) (۳) . ورد بالمنع بل كان من الجن ففسق عن أمر ربه وإنما أدرج في الملائكة على سبيل التغليب لكونه جنياً واحداً مغموراً فيما بينهم، لا يقال معنى قوله : «كان من الجن صار أو كان طائفة من من الملائكة مسماة بالجن، شأنهم الاستكبار، لانا نقول : هذا مع كونه كلاماً على السند خلاف الظاهر.
"What prevented you from prostrating when I commanded you?" (1). (2) And by the proof of the validity of excluding him from them in His statement, the Exalted: "So they prostrated except Iblis" and His statement, the Exalted: "So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis; he refused to be among the prostrating ones" (3). And it is replied with the denial; rather, he was from the jinn and thus disobeyed the command of his Lord. He was only included among the angels by way of predominance, because he was a single jinn submerged among them. Do not say that the meaning of His statement "he was from the jinn" is that he became or was a group of the angels called 'jinn', whose characteristic is arrogance. For we say: This, besides being a statement upon a chain, is contrary to the apparent.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector uses the fact that Iblis was commanded with the angels to prostrate and is excluded from them in the Quran to argue that Iblis was an angel who disobeyed, thus breaking angelic infallibility. The response denies this by asserting that Iblis was from the jinn, not angels, and his inclusion among angels in the command is by predominance (taghlib). The author also refutes a potential alternative interpretation that Iblis was part of a subset of angels called 'jinn'. This alternative is rejected because it is contrary to the apparent meaning of the text.

Key Terms
استثنائه
تغليب
جن
ملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Iblis was an angel who disobeyed, which would imply angels can sin.
Correction: Iblis was from the jinn, not angels, as clarified by the verse 'he was from the jinn'. His inclusion with angels was by predominance (taghlib).

Checkpoint
What is the main argument used to refute the claim that Iblis was an angel?
A) He was from the jinn.
B) He was a devil.
C) He was originally an angel who fell.
D) He was not included in the command.

Key Takeaway
Iblis was not an angel but a jinn; his inclusion among the angels in the command to prostrate was by predominance (taghlib).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Iblis was commanded to prostrate but refused, think of a command of Allah that you know but have not fully obeyed. What exception have you made in your heart that allows you to delay or ignore it? Will you commit to acting on it today?
?
The author rejects an interpretation because it is 'contrary to the apparent' and based on weak transmission. When you face a doubt about your faith, do you turn to the clear verses of the Quran and authentic teachings, or do you follow weak opinions that ease your conscience? What is one doubt you need to resolve by returning to the clear source?
?
Iblis was included among the angels by predominance, but his inner reality was rebellion. Are you in a community of believers while your heart harbors rebellion against Allah? What is the state of your sincerity, and what will you do today to align your heart with your outward worship?

Angels' Question: Criticism or Inquiry?
The author defends the angels' question as inquiry, not sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the angels' question about the vicegerent was not a sin but a request for wisdom.

Core Idea
Questioning God's wisdom is not sin when seeking understanding.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid tackles a key objection: did the angels sin by questioning God's decision to create a vicegerent? The author argues that their question was an inquiry into divine wisdom, not criticism. This lesson unpacks that argument, showing how even angels can ask for deeper understanding without compromising their infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the claim that the angels' words constitute backbiting and self-praise, which would break infallibility.
The objection is that the angels seemed to criticize God's plan.
2
Follow the answer
The author distinguishes between backbiting (showing defect) and seeking wisdom. The angels' purpose was wonder and inquiry.
They knew of human corruption through divine notification, the Preserved Tablet, or analogy.
3
Address counter-arguments
Two 'la yuqalu' rebuttals are given. The first concerns God's command to 'inform Me of names'; the second concerns infallibility. See how the author refutes them.
The error of not knowing full wisdom does not negate infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني. أن قولهم في جواب : إني جاعل في الأرض خليفة : ( أتجعل فيها من يفسد فيها ويسفك الدماء ونحن نسبح بحمدك ونقدس لك (٤) غتياب للخليفة واستبعاد لفعل الله تعالى بحيث يشبه صورة الإنكار بمعنى أنه لا ينبغي أن يكون، واتباع للظن، ورجم بالغيب فيما لا يليق وإعجاب بأنفسهم، وتزكية .لها. وأمثال هذه تخل بالعصمة لا محالة. والجواب : ان الاغتياب إنما يكون حيث الغرض إظهار منقصة الغير، والتزكية حيث الغرض إظهار منقبة النفس. ولا يتصور ذلك بالنسبة إلى علام الغيوب، بل الغرض التعجب والاستفسار عن حكمة استخلاف من يتصف بما لا يليق بذلك، مع وجود الأولى والأليق . وإنما علموا ذلك بإعلام من الله تعالى، أو مشاهدة من اللوح، أو مقايسة بين الجن والإنس بمشاركتهما في الشهوة والغضب المفضيين إلى الفساد وسفك الدماء. لا يقال قوله تعالى أنبئوني بأسماء هؤلاء إن كنتم صادقين اي في أني استخلف من يتصف بما ذكرتم ينافي كون ذلك متحققاً معلوماً لهم بإعلام من الله تعالى، أو إخبار أو بمشاهدة من اللوح، لأنا نقول : المعنى إن كنتم صادقين) (۱) في أني أستخلف من يتصف بذلك من غير حكم، ومصالح ، وصفات تلائم الاستخلاف، إذ التعجب إنما يكون عند ذلك. ولذا قال في الرد عليهم إني أعلم ما لا تعلمون) (٢) . إشارة إلى تلك الحكم والمصالح . لا يقال ففيه دلالة على نفي العصمة بإثبات الكذب من الجملة لأنا نقول: هذا القدر من الخطأ والسهو لا ينافي العصمة، ولا يوجب المعصية
Second: That their statement in response to 'I am placing a vicegerent on earth': 'Will You place therein one who causes corruption and sheds blood, while we glorify Your praise and sanctify You?' (4) is backbiting of the vicegerent and considering God's act far-fetched, resembling a form of denial meaning that it should not be, following conjecture, shooting at the unseen regarding what is not fitting, and self-admiration and self-praise. Such things undoubtedly detract from infallibility. The answer: Backbiting only occurs where the purpose is to show the defect of another, and self-praise where the purpose is to show one's own merit. This is not conceivable with respect to the Knower of the Unseen; rather the purpose was wonder and inquiry about the wisdom of appointing a successor characterized by what is not fitting, given the existence of what is better and more fitting. They only knew that by notification from God, or observation of the Preserved Tablet, or analogical comparison between jinn and humans due to their sharing desire and anger which lead to corruption and bloodshed. Do not say that His statement 'Inform Me of the names of these if you are truthful' meaning that I appoint a successor characterized by what you mentioned contradicts that this was realized and known to them by notification from God or report or observation of the Tablet. For we say: The meaning is 'if you are truthful' in that I appoint a successor characterized by that without wisdom, benefits, and attributes suitable for succession, for wonder only occurs at that. Hence He said in response to them 'I know what you do not know' (2), indicating those wisdoms and benefits. Do not say that this indicates a negation of infallibility by establishing falsehood in part. For we say: This amount of error and forgetfulness does not negate infallibility nor necessitate sin.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage handles the second objection: that the angels' question to God about creating a vicegerent who sheds blood was a form of backbiting, which would be a sin. The author explains that the angels' purpose was not to find fault but to seek wisdom. They knew of human corruption by divine notification, the Preserved Tablet, or analogy. The answer also addresses the Quranic verse where God asks them to inform Him of names, clarifying it means they were not truly aware of all wisdoms. Finally, this level of error (mistaking the wisdom) is not contrary to infallibility.

Key Terms
غتياب
تزكية
عصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The angels sinned by questioning God's decision.
Correction: Their purpose was to inquire about wisdom, not criticize, and such inquiry does not violate infallibility.

Checkpoint
What was the purpose of the angels' question according to the author?
A) To criticize God's decision.
B) To seek wisdom and understanding.
C) To express jealousy.
D) To test God.

Key Takeaway
Questioning divine actions for understanding is not a sin when done in humility and without ill intent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation that seems unjust or lacking wisdom from God — like the angels initially saw — do you rush to judgment or do you pause to seek understanding of the hidden wisdoms? What does your immediate reaction reveal about your trust in God's wisdom?
?
The author says that backbiting and self-praise are defined by their intent. Think of your own conversations: how often do you complain about others under the guise of 'discussing' or 'analyzing'? Can you honestly say your intent is pure inquiry, or is there a veiled sense of superiority?
?
The angels, despite their high status, made a mistake in understanding — but it did not diminish their virtue or closeness to God. What mistake in your own understanding of Islam or God's plan are you holding onto out of pride? Are you willing to humbly learn, like the angels did, that God knows what you do not know?

Objection and Answer: The Story of Harut and Marut
The author refutes the objection that angels Harut and Marut sinned by teaching sorcery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends the sinlessness of angels against the objection of Harut and Marut, explaining that their actions were a divine trial and their punishment a rebuke.

Core Idea
Angels cannot sin; Harut and Marut were a divine test, not sinners.

One of the strongest objections to the sinlessness of angels is the story of Harut and Marut, who are said to have practiced sorcery and been punished. The author addresses this by reinterpreting the narrative: they did not sin but were instruments of trial, and any punishment was merely a gentle rebuke. This passage clarifies the theological boundaries regarding angelic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the core argument: what is claimed against angels and how it is refuted.
Notice the phrase 'إنما نحن فتنة' – 'We are only a trial'.
2
Analyze the reinterpretation
The author denies that Harut and Marut actually practiced sorcery or believed in its effect. Instead, they were a test from God. Identify how this preserves angelic sinlessness.
3
Examine the nature of their punishment
The punishment is described as 'معاتبة' (rebuke), similar to prophets' slips. This is distinct from punishment for sin. Understand the difference.
This shows that even a slip is not a sin for angels.
4
Consider the Jewish attribution
The author attributes the claim that angels can sin to the Jews. Reflect on why this matters for the defense of orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - قصة هاروت وماروت ملكين ببابل يعذبان لارتكابهما السحر. (۳) والجواب منع ارتكابهما العمل بالسحر، واعتقاد تأثيره، بل أنزل الله تعالى عليهما السحر ابتلاء للناس، فمن تعلمه و عمل به فكافر. ومن تجنبه أو تعلمه ليتوقاه ولا يغتر به فهو مؤمن وهما كانا يعظان الناس ويقولان : إنما نحن فتنة (٣) للناس وابتلاء، فلا تكفروا أي لا تعتقدوا ولا تعملوا فإن ذلك كفر. وتعذيبهما إنما هو على وجه المعاتبة كما تعاتب الأنبياء على السهو والزلة من غير ارتكاب منهما لكبيرة فضلاً عن كفر ، واعتقاد سحر أو عمل به . واليهود هم الذين يدعون أن الواحد من الملك قد يرتكب الكبيرة فيعاقبه الله بالمسخ.
Third: The story of Harut and Marut, two angels in Babylon being punished for practicing sorcery. (3) The answer: denying that they practiced sorcery or believed in its effect; rather, God revealed sorcery to them as a trial for mankind. Whoever learns it and practices it is a disbeliever; whoever avoids it or learns it to guard against it and not be deceived by it is a believer. They were warning people and saying: 'We are only a trial (3) for people and a test, so do not disbelieve' meaning do not believe or practice for that is disbelief. Their punishment is only in the way of rebuke, as prophets are rebuked for forgetfulness and slip, without them committing a major sin, let alone disbelief, belief in sorcery or practicing it. The Jews are the ones who claim that an angel may commit a major sin and God punishes him by transformation.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage addresses the third objection: that two angels, Harut and Marut, sinned by practicing sorcery and were punished. The response denies that they practiced sorcery or believed in its effect. Rather, God used them as a test; they warned people. Their punishment was a mild rebuke, not for sin but for a slip. The author attributes the claim that angels can sin to the Jews.

Key Terms
هاروت وماروت
سحر
فتنة
معاتبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels Harut and Marut sinned by practicing sorcery.
Correction: The author clarifies they did not practice sorcery or believe in its effect; they were a test from God, and their punishment was a rebuke for a slip, not a sin.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, why were Harut and Marut punished?
A) For teaching sorcery.
B) For a minor slip (zalla).
C) For disbelief.
D) They were not punished at all.

Key Takeaway
The story of Harut and Marut does not contradict angelic sinlessness because they were a divine test and their punishment was merely a rebuke, not a penalty for sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered a 'small' sin so insignificant that you thought it wouldn't affect your faith? How does the distinction between a rebuke for a slip and punishment for a major sin challenge your attitude towards minor sins? What step will you take today to guard against even the smallest disobedience?
?
When you see others involved in forbidden practices like sorcery or superstitious beliefs, do you recognize that they are being tested, or do you feel self-righteous? How can you, like Harut and Marut, warn them with humility and without judgment?
?
If you were to study something potentially harmful like sorcery to protect yourself from it, would your intention be pure enough to be considered a believer? Or is there a hidden curiosity that could lead you astray? Be honest: what is the state of your heart when learning or dabbling in worldly matters?

Wali and Karamah: Definitions and Mu'tazila Objections
Definition of wali and karamah with refutation of Mu'tazila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of wali and karamah, their permissibility, and the response to Mu'tazila objections.

Core Idea
Karamah of saints is distinct from prophetic miracles because intent and claim differ.

This lesson establishes the theological concept of sainthood (wilaya) and the miraculous deeds (karamat) performed by saints. The author defines these terms and then addresses objections from the Mu'tazila who argue that karamah would undermine the uniqueness of prophetic miracles. Through definitions and examples, the author defends the possibility of karamah while preserving the distinction between prophet and saint.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Familiarize yourself with the key terms and the flow of the argument.
Notice the author uses a compact style.
2
Identify the definitions of wali and karamah
Pinpoint the definitions: wali is one who knows God and turns away from other than Him; karamah is a supernatural event without a claim to prophethood, permissible and of the same genus as miracles.
Memorize the Arabic terms: الولي, الكرامة.
3
Note the examples given
The author cites Maryam, Asif, the People of the Cave, and widespread accounts from early Muslims. These support the occurrence of karamah.
These are well-known cases from Quran and tradition.
4
Understand the Mu'tazila objections and the author's answers
List the four objections: confusion of prophet/saint, frequent breach of natural law, difficulty proving prophethood, and diminishing prophet status. Then see how the author counters each.
Focus on the distinction: karamah lacks a claim to prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الثامن - (الولي هو العارف بالله تعالى الصارف همته عما سواه. والكرامة ظهور أمر خارق للعادة من قبله بلا دعوى النبوة وهي جائزة ولو بقصد الولي ومن جنس المعجزات لشمول قدرة الله تعالى. وواقعة كقصة مريم، وآصف، وأصحاب الكهف، وما تواتر جنسه من الصحابة والتابعين، وكثير من الصالحين وخالفت المعتزلة لأنها توجب التباس النبي بغيره، إذ الفارق هو المعجزة، والخروج عن بعض العادة لكثرة الأولياء، وانسداد باب إثبات النبوة لاحتمال أن تكون المعجزة إكراماً، لا تصديقاً، والإخلال بعظم قدر الأنبياء لمشاركة الأولياء. والجواب أن الكرامة لا تقارن دعوى النبوة، وكثرتها تكون استمرار نقض العادة، والمقارنة للدعوى تفيد القطع بالصدق عادة والكرامة تزيد جلالة قدر
He said: The Eighth Chapter - (The wali (saint) is the one who knows God the Most High and turns his concern away from other than Him. And the karamah (miracle of a saint) is the appearance of a matter that breaks the ordinary course of events from him without a claim to prophethood, and it is permissible even if intended by the wali and of the same genus as miracles (mu'jizat) due to the inclusiveness of God's power. And examples include the story of Maryam, Asif, the People of the Cave, and what has been recurrently transmitted of its kind from the Companions, the Followers, and many of the righteous. And the Mu'tazila opposed (this) because it would cause confusion between the prophet and others, since the differentiator is the miracle, and (because of) the departure from some aspects of the ordinary course of events due to the abundance of awliya, and the blocking of the door of establishing prophethood due to the probability that the miracle might be an honor (ikram) not a confirmation (tasdiq), and (because of) diminishing the great status of the prophets due to the sharing of the awliya. The answer: The karamah is not accompanied by a claim to prophethood, and its abundance results in the continuation of the breaking of the ordinary course (of events), and the accompaniment of the claim provides certainty of truthfulness ordinarily, and the karamah increases the majesty of the status...
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage defines the wali as one who knows God and turns his concern away from other than Him. Karamah is a supernatural event that occurs through a wali without a claim to prophethood. It is permissible and similar to miracles in kind. Examples from the Quran and tradition are given. The Mu'tazila raise four objections: (1) confusion between prophet and saint, (2) frequent departures from the ordinary course, (3) difficulty in proving prophethood if miracles can be honorific, (4) diminishing the status of prophets. The answer: karamah is never accompanied by a claim to prophethood, its frequency does not undermine the ordinary course, the accompaniment of a claim to prophethood provides certainty, and karamah actually increases the majesty of the prophets.

Key Terms
الولي
الكرامة
المعجزة
المعتزلة
الإكرام
التصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karamah is the same as a prophetic miracle, so saints are like prophets.
Correction: Karamah is of the same genus but lacks a claim to prophethood. The claim is what distinguishes a prophetic miracle (mu'jiza) as a confirmation of truth.

Checkpoint
What is the primary argument of the Mu'tazila against the occurrence of karamah?
A) That karamah is impossible because it would contradict natural laws.
B) That karamah would cause confusion between the prophet and the saint because the distinguishing sign is the miracle.
C) That karamah would diminish the status of the prophets.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Saints can perform supernatural acts (karamat) that are distinct from prophetic miracles due to the absence of a claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever longed for a spiritual experience or miracle to prove your own worth before God, rather than to draw nearer to Him? How can you purify your intention so that every good thing becomes worship, not self-display?
?
The Mu'tazila feared that karamah would blur the line between saint and prophet. In your own life, do you ever confuse worldly admiration with true spiritual station? What steps can you take to seek only Allah's approval, not people's praise?
?
The author said karamah increases the majesty of the prophets. Do you truly honor the Prophet ﷺ in your daily choices—your speech, your priorities, your time? Or have you allowed complacency to dim your reverence? Write one concrete action you will take today to show that honor.

Karamat al-Awliya: Views and Conditions
Discussion of majority view, Mu'tazila view, and conditions for karamah of saints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic positions on karamat al-awliya, the conditions proposed by some scholars, and the definitive criterion that distinguishes them from prophetic miracles.

Core Idea
Karamat are real but cannot be confused with prophethood—the absence of a claim is key.

This passage from Imam al-Haramayn's Sharh al-Maqasid presents a nuanced discussion on the permissibility and nature of karamat (supernatural acts performed by saints). While the majority of Muslims affirm them, the Mu'tazila deny them entirely. Among those who accept karamat, there are disagreements about conditions. The author then gives the preferred view, emphasizing that the only essential distinction from prophetic miracles is the absence of a claim to prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's progression.
Notice the shift from reporting opinions to stating the preferred view.
2
Identify the three main views
Identify the majority view (permissibility), the Mu'tazila view (forbidden), and the conditions set by some who permit.
The conditions are: not by saint's choice, not based on claim, not same kind as prophetic miracles.
3
Understand the Imam's critique and resolution
See how Imam al-Haramayn rejects the proposed conditions as unsound and declares that all supernatural events are permissible as karamah.
The key point: the sole distinction from miracles is the absence of a prophethood claim.
4
Apply the distinction
Consider how this principle guards against false prophets and ensures sainthood remains distinct from prophethood.
Claiming prophethood makes one an enemy of Allah, not a recipient of karamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب جمهور المسلمين إلى جواز كرامة الأولياء، ومنعه أكثر المعتزلة، والأستاذ ابو إسحاق يميل إلى قريب من مذهبهم. كذا قال إمام الحرمين، ثم المجوزون ذهب بعضهم إلى امتناع كون الكرامة بقصد واختيار من الولي وبعضهم إلى امتناع كونها على قضية الدعوى، حتى لو ادعى الولي الولاية . واعتقد بخوارق العادات ، لم يجز، ولم يقع ، بل ربما يسقط عن مرتبة الولاية. وبعضهم إلى امتناع كونها من جنس ما وقع معجزة لنبي كانفلاق البحر، وانقلاب العصا، وإحياء الموتى. قالوا وبهذه الجهات تمتاز عن المعجزات وقال الإمام هذه الطرق غير سديدة والمرضي عندنا تجويز جملة خوارق العادات في معرض الكرامات. وإنما تمتاز عن المعجزات بخلوها عن دعوى النبوة، حتى لو ادعى الولي النبوة صار عدواً الله ، لا يستحق الكرامة، بل اللعنة والإهانة.
The majority of Muslims have gone to the permissibility of the karamah of saints, and most of the Mu'tazila forbade it, and al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq inclined close to their view. Such said Imam al-Haramayn. Then among those who permit, some went to the impossibility of the karamah being by the intention and choice of the saint, and some to the impossibility of it being based on a claim; even if the saint claims sainthood and believes in supernatural events, it is not permissible and does not occur, and he may even fall from the rank of sainthood. And some to the impossibility of it being of the same kind as a miracle that occurred for a prophet, like the splitting of the sea, the transformation of the staff, and reviving the dead. They said: by these aspects they are distinguished from miracles. And the Imam said: these ways are not sound, and the approved view with us is the permissibility of all supernatural events in the context of karamat. They are only distinguished from miracles by being free of the claim to prophethood. Even if the saint claims prophethood, he becomes an enemy of Allah, not deserving of karamah, but rather curse and humiliation.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage discusses the views on karamah. The majority of Muslims allow it, but most Mu'tazila deny it. Some who permit it set conditions: (1) it cannot be by the saint's intention and choice, (2) it cannot be in response to a claim of sainthood (otherwise the saint might fall from sainthood), (3) it cannot be of the same type as a prophet's miracle (like splitting the sea). However, the author's own school (the Imam) rejects these restrictions and holds that all supernatural events are permissible as karamah, and the sole distinguishing factor from mu'jizah is the absence of a claim to prophethood. If a saint claims prophethood, he becomes an enemy of Allah.

Key Terms

المعتزلة
دعوى الولاية
المعجزة
اللعنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saints can perform miracles like prophets, but the defining line is the claim to prophethood.
Correction: The passage clarifies that karamah is distinguished from mu'jizah solely by being free of a claim to prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the passage, what distinguishes a karamah from a mu'jizah?
A) Karamah is weaker.
B) Karamah is not a violation of norms.
C) Karamah is free from a claim to prophethood.
D) Karamah is only for saints.

Key Takeaway
The sole distinction between karamah and mu'jizah is the absence or presence of a claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Imagine you witness someone performing apparent miracles and they begin to claim spiritual authority beyond the Prophetic model. Would you have the courage to reject them, knowing that a false claim to prophethood makes them an enemy of Allah? Examine your own vulnerability to being swayed by extraordinary displays.

Scholarly Positions on Karamat and the Preferred View
Disagreement on karamat and the Imam's resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement on karamat and the distinguishing criterion according to the preferred view.

Core Idea
The only valid distinction between a saint's miracle and a prophet's miracle is the absence of a claim to prophethood.

Muslim scholars have debated whether saints can perform miracles. This passage presents the majority view, the Mu'tazila opposition, and various restrictions proposed by those who permit karamat, culminating in the Imam's preferred view that all extraordinary events are permissible as karamat as long as no prophethood is claimed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main positions
Read the passage to find the two main camps: the majority who permit karamat and the Mu'tazila who forbid it. Also note that al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq inclines toward the Mu'tazila.
The majority view is the starting point.
2
Examine the three restrictions
Among those who permit karamat, some placed restrictions: the karama cannot be by the saint's intention, cannot be in response to claiming sainthood, and cannot be of the same type as a prophetic miracle. List these three.
These restrictions were meant to distinguish karamat from mu'jizat.
3
Understand Imam al-Haramayn's rejection
The Imam declares these restrictions unsound. Notice his phrase 'these ways are not sound'. He then gives the approved view.
The Imam's authority is al-Juwayni.
4
Grasp the final criterion
According to the preferred view, karamat are distinguished from mu'jizat only by the lack of a claim to prophethood. If a saint claims prophethood, he becomes an enemy of God.
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب جمهور المسلمين إلى جواز كرامة الأولياء، ومنعه أكثر المعتزلة، والأستاذ ابو إسحاق يميل إلى قريب من مذهبهم. كذا قال إمام الحرمين، ثم المجوزون ذهب بعضهم إلى امتناع كون الكرامة بقصد واختيار من الولي وبعضهم إلى امتناع كونها على قضية الدعوى، حتى لو ادعى الولي الولاية . واعتقد بخوارق العادات ، لم يجز، ولم يقع ، بل ربما يسقط عن مرتبة الولاية. وبعضهم إلى امتناع كونها من جنس ما وقع معجزة لنبي كانفلاق البحر، وانقلاب العصا، وإحياء الموتى. قالوا وبهذه الجهات تمتاز عن المعجزات وقال الإمام هذه الطرق غير سديدة والمرضي عندنا تجويز جملة خوارق العادات في معرض الكرامات. وإنما تمتاز عن المعجزات بخلوها عن دعوى النبوة، حتى لو ادعى الولي النبوة صار عدواً الله ، لا يستحق الكرامة، بل اللعنة والإهانة.
And the majority of Muslims went to the permissibility of karamat of the awliya (saints), and most Mu'tazila forbade it, and al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq inclined close to their doctrine. Thus said Imam al-Haramayn. Then those who permit, some of them went to the impossibility of the karama being by the intention and choice of the wali, and some to the impossibility of it being in response to a claim, such that if the wali claimed wilayah (sainthood) and believed in extraordinary events, it would not be permissible and would not occur, rather he might fall from the rank of wilayah. And some to the impossibility of it being of the same type as a mu'jiza of a prophet, such as splitting of the sea, transformation of a staff, and reviving the dead. They said: by these aspects it is distinguished from mu'jizat. And Imam said: these ways are not sound; the approved view with us is the permissibility of all extraordinary events in the context of karamat. They are distinguished from mu'jizat only by their lack of a claim to prophethood, to the point that if the wali claimed prophethood, he becomes an enemy of God, not deserving karama, rather curse and disgrace.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents the scholarly disagreement on karamat and then gives the preferred view of the Imam (likely al-Juwayni). It states that the majority of Muslims permit karamat of saints, while most Mu'tazila forbid them; al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq (al-Isfarayini) inclines toward the Mu'tazila position. Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) reports this. Among those who permit karamat, there are three further restrictions: (1) some say the karama cannot happen by the saint's intention and choice; (2) some say it cannot happen in response to a claim of sainthood—if a saint claims to be a saint and expects miracles, it would not occur and he might lose his rank; (3) some say it cannot be of the same type as a prophetic miracle (e.g., splitting the sea). These are proposed as ways to distinguish karamat from mu'jizat. However, the Imam rejects these restrictions as unsound. The approved view is to permit all extraordinary events as karamat, distinguishing them from mu'jizat solely by the absence of a claim to prophethood. If a saint claims prophethood, he becomes an enemy of God and deserves curse and disgrace, not karama.

Key Terms
كرامة (karama)
ولي (wali)
معجزة (mu'jiza)
معتزلة (Mu'tazila)
إمام الحرمين (Imam al-Haramayn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karama can be of the same type as a prophetic miracle or can be claimed by the saint.
Correction: The Imam holds that karamat can be of any type, but they are distinguished solely by the absence of a claim to prophethood, and any such claim would make the person an enemy of God.

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, how is a karama distinguished from a mu'jiza?
A) Karama is weaker in power.
B) Karama is not of the same type as prophetic miracles.
C) Karama lacks a claim to prophethood.
D) Karama is only for saints, not prophets.

Key Takeaway
The approved view permits all extraordinary events as karamat, distinguishing them from prophetic miracles only by the lack of a claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever experienced something spiritually uplifting and felt a secret pride, thinking 'God has favored me specially'? How does this lesson's emphasis on the sole distinction being the claim to prophethood expose the danger of even subtle spiritual arrogance? What step will you take today to ensure your heart remains humble before God?
?
The passage states that if a saint claims prophethood, he becomes an enemy of God. But more subtly, do you ever find yourself enjoying recognition from others for your religious knowledge or piety—essentially claiming a spiritual status? What would it look like to genuinely purify your intentions and never let your heart rest on being seen as a 'saint'?
?
Consider the three restrictions that some scholars proposed to distinguish karamat. The Imam rejects all but one. Why do you think it is easier for humans to multiply distinctions (like 'this miracle is from God, this is from a saint') rather than to simply submit to the sole criterion of prophethood? Where in your own life do you add unnecessary conditions to God's mercy or grace, thinking you must be a certain type of person to deserve His favor?

Refutation of Views on Sainthood and Prophethood
States and refutes three erroneous views on the relationship between sainthood and prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three erroneous views on the relationship between sainthood and prophethood and why they are rejected by Sunni consensus.

Core Idea
Sainthood does not surpass prophethood; the prophet's rank is unique and superior.

After establishing the correct position on sainthood and prophethood, the author addresses three false claims that have emerged among different groups. These claims undermine the unique status of prophets and the clarity of divine law. The passage presents each view and refutes them with clear arguments and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source text once, then the translation. Note the structure: correct position, then three false views, then refutations.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three erroneous views
Find where the author mentions the Karramiyya, some Sufis, and libertines/atheists. Note what each group claims about sainthood relative to prophethood.
These are the three views that are refuted.
3
Understand the refutations
Focus on how the author refutes the first two views. The refutation of the third (libertines) is implied by the correct position and the refutation of the first two.
The refutations rely on the prophet's unique perfections.
4
Reflect on the consensus
Note that the author declares all three views 'corrupt by the consensus of Muslims.' Consider why these views are considered beyond acceptable differences.
Consensus (ijma') is a strong evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : خاتمة (لا يبلغ الولي درجة النبي ولا يسقط عنه التكاليف بكمال الولاية، ولا تكون ولاية غير النبي أفضل من النبوة، وإنما الكلام في ولايته، فقيل : هي أفضل لما فيها من معنى القرب والاختصاص، وقيل: بل نبوته لما فيها من الوساطة بين الحق والخلق والقيام بمصالح الدارين مع شرف مشاهدة الملك . حكي عن بعض الكرامية أن الولي قد يبلغ درجة النبي، بل أعلى . وعن بعض الصوفية أن الولاية أفضل من النبوة، لأنها تنبىء عن القرب والكرامة كما هو شأن خواص الملك والمقربين منه، والنبوة عن الإنباء والتبليغ ، كما هو حال من أرسله الملك إلى الرعايا لتبليغ أحكامه. إلا أن الولي لا يبلغ درجة النبي، لأن النبوة لا تكون بدون الولاية وعن أهل الإباحة والإلحاد أن الولي إذا بلغ الغاية في المحبة وصفاء القلب، وكمال الإخلاص ، سقط عنه الأمر والنهي، ولم يضره الذنب ، ولا يدخل النار بارتكاب الكبيرة والكل فاسد بإجماع المسلمين. والأول خاصة بأن النبي مع ما له من شرف الولاية، معصوم عن المعاصي، مأمون عن سوء العاقبة بحكم النصوص القاطعة ، مشرف بالوحي ومشاهدة الملك، مبعوث لإصلاح حال العالم ونظام أمر المعاش والمعاد.. إلى غير ذلك من الكمالات. والثاني بأن النبوة تنبىء عن البعثة والتبليغ من الحق إلى الخلق . ففيها ملاحظة للجانبين. ويتضمن قرب الولاية وشرفها لا محالة فلا تقصر عن مرتبة ولاية غير الأنبياء لأنها لا تكون على غاية الكمال، لأن علامة ذلك نيل مرتبة النبوة .
He said: Conclusion (A saint does not reach the degree of a prophet, nor are obligations removed from him by the perfection of sainthood, nor is the sainthood of other than a prophet better than prophethood. Rather the discussion is about his own sainthood. It was said: his sainthood is better because of the meaning of nearness and special distinction in it; and it was said: rather his prophethood is better because of the mediation between truth and creation and undertaking the interests of both worlds along with the honor of witnessing the angel. It was narrated from some of the Karramiyya that the saint may reach the degree of a prophet, even higher. And from some of the Sufis that sainthood is better than prophethood, because it indicates nearness and honor, as is the case of the king's elite and close ones, while prophethood indicates announcement and delivery, as is the case of one sent by the king to the subjects to deliver his rulings. However, the saint does not reach the degree of the prophet, because prophethood cannot be without sainthood. And from the libertines and atheists that if the saint reaches the ultimate in love, purity of heart, and perfection of sincerity, command and prohibition fall away from him, sin does not harm him, and he does not enter the Fire for committing a major sin. All of this is corrupt by the consensus of Muslims. The first [view] is specifically [refuted] because the prophet, along with his honor of sainthood, is infallible from sins, secure from evil end by definitive texts, honored by revelation and witnessing the angel, sent for reforming the state of the world and ordering the affairs of livelihood and afterlife, besides other perfections. And the second [view] is [refuted] because prophethood indicates sending and delivery from the Truth to creation. So it takes into account both sides. It necessarily includes the nearness and honor of sainthood, so it does not fall short of the rank of sainthood of non-prophets, because that [sainthood] is not at the ultimate perfection, since the sign of that is attaining the rank of prophethood.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of three erroneous views concerning the relationship between sainthood (wilaya) and prophethood (nubuwwa). The author begins by stating the correct position: a saint never reaches the rank of a prophet, obligations are not lifted due to perfection of sainthood, and the sainthood of a non-prophet is not superior to prophethood. Then he presents the disputed issue among scholars regarding the prophet himself: whether his sainthood or his prophethood is superior. Two opinions are cited but not settled here. Next, three false views are mentioned: (1) the Karramiyya claim that a saint can reach or surpass a prophet's rank; (2) some Sufis claim that sainthood is superior to prophethood; (3) libertines claim that obligations drop for the perfect saint. The author declares all three corrupt by consensus. Then he specifically refutes the first two: The first is refuted by the prophet's unique perfections (infallibility, revelation, mission). The second is refuted by noting that prophethood inherently includes sainthood but also adds the role of mediation and mission, thus it is superior. The refutation of the third view comes later.

Key Terms
الولي
النبي
الولاية
النبوة
الكرامية
الصوفية
الإباحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that sainthood is superior to prophethood because of nearness to God.
Correction: Prophethood includes that nearness and adds the immense honor of being a messenger, making it superior.

Checkpoint
Which group claimed that a saint can reach or exceed the rank of a prophet?
A) Sufis
B) Karramiyya
C) Libertines
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The prophet's rank is unique and superior to any saint; prophethood encompasses sainthood and adds the honor of divine mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The author refutes the view that sainthood is better than prophethood because prophethood includes service to creation. Are you more focused on personal spiritual 'nearness' to Allah, or on serving His creation as the prophets did? What concrete act of service can you do today that shifts your focus from self to others?

The Debate: Prophethood or Sainthood?
Author presents two opinions on prophethood vs. sainthood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two opinions regarding the superiority of prophethood versus sainthood in the Prophet.

Core Idea
The superiority of prophethood or sainthood is debated based on their distinct meanings.

This lesson introduces a classical theological hesitation: is the Prophet's prophethood or his sainthood superior? The author presents two perspectives, each highlighting different aspects of the Prophet's role. One emphasizes mediation and service, the other closeness and exclusivity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how the author presents two contrasting views.
The passage begins with the hesitation before giving the two opinions.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find the phrase for each opinion and note the reasoning given for each. The first opinion favors prophethood, the second favors sainthood.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Ask yourself: why would mediation and witnessing the angel make prophethood superior? And why would closeness and exclusivity make sainthood superior?
This prepares you for the qualified statement in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو يقع تردد في أن نبوة النبي أفضل أم ولايته. فمن قائل بالأول لما في النبوة من معنى الوساطة بين الجانبين والقيام بمصالح الخلق في الدارين، مع شرف مشاهدة الملك. ومن مائل إلى الثاني لما في الولاية من معنى القرب والاختصاص الذي يكون في النبي في غاية الكمال، بخلاف ولاية غير النبي. وفي كلام بعض العرفاء أن ما قيل الولاية أفضل من النبوة لا يصح مطلقاً، وليس من الأدب إطلاق القول به، بل لا بد من التقييد، وهو أن ولاية النبي أفضل من نبوته، لأن نبوة التشريع متعلقة بمصلحة الوقت والولاية لا تعلق لها بوقت دون وقت، بل قام سلطانها إلى قيام الساعة، بخلاف النبوة فإنها مختومة بمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم من حيث ظاهرها الذي هو الإنباء، وإن كانت دائمة من حيث باطنها الذي هو الولاية، أعني التصرف في الخلق بالحق، فإن الأولياء من أمة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم تصرف ولايته بهم، يتصرف في الخلق بالحق إلى قيام الساعة، ولهذا كانت علامتهم المتابعة. إذ ليس الولي إلا مظهر تصرف النبي. وأما بطلان القول بسقوط الأمر والنهي فلعموم الخطابات، ولأن أكمل الناس في المحبة والإخلاص هم الأنبياء، سيما حبيب الله، مع أن التكاليف في حقهم أتم وأكمل، حتى يعاتبون بأدنى زلة، بل بترك الأفضل. نعم حكي عن بعض الأولياء أنه استعفى الله عن التكاليف، وسأله الإعتاق عن ظواهر العبادات، فأجابه إلى ذلك بأن سلبه العقل الذي هو مناط التكليف، ومع ذلك كان من علو المرتبة على ما كان. وأنت خبير بأن العارف لا يسأم من العبادة، ولا يفتر في الطاعة ولا يسأل الهبوط من أوج الكمال إلى حضيض النقصان، والنزول من معارج الملك إلى منازل الحيوان، بل ربما يحصل له كمال الانجذاب إلى عالم القدس والاستغراق في ملاحظة جناب الحق، بحيث يذهب عن هذا العالم، ويخل بالتكاليف من غير تأثم بذلك لكونه في حكم غير المكلف كالنائم، وذلك لعجزه عن مراعاة الأمرين وملاحظة الجانبين، فربما يسأل دوام تلك الحالة، وعدم العود إلى عالم الظاهر، وهذا الذهول هو الجنون الذي ربما يرجح على بعض العقول، والمتسمون به هم المسمون بمجانين العقلاء. وبهذا يظهر فضل الأنبياء على الأولياء، فإنهم مع أن استغراقهم أكمل، وانجذابهم أشمل لا يخلون بأدنى طاعة، ولا يذهلون من هذا الجانب ساعة، لأن قوتهم القدسية من الكمال بحيث لا يشغلها شاغل عن ذلك الجناب، ولهذا ينعى عليهم أدنى زلة عن منهج الصواب.
There occurs hesitation whether the Prophet's prophethood is better or his sainthood. Some say the first because in prophethood there is the meaning of mediation between the two sides and undertaking the interests of creation in both abodes, along with the honor of witnessing the angel. Some incline to the second because in sainthood there is the meaning of proximity and specification which exists in the Prophet in utmost perfection, unlike the sainthood of other than the Prophet. In the speech of some mystics that what was said 'sainthood is better than prophethood' is not absolutely correct, and it is not of proper etiquette to utter it absolutely, rather it must be qualified: that the Prophet's sainthood is better than his prophethood, because legislative prophethood is connected to the benefit of the time, while sainthood has no connection to one time over another; rather its authority stands until the Hour, unlike prophethood, for it is sealed with Muhammad (peace be upon him) in terms of its outward aspect which is conveying news, even if it is permanent in terms of its inward aspect which is sainthood, namely acting upon creation with truth. For the saints of the nation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) manifest his authority through them; he acts upon creation with truth until the Hour, and therefore their mark is [the Prophet's] following. For the saint is nothing but a manifestation of the Prophet's action. As for the invalidity of the saying that commands and prohibitions are dropped, it is due to the generality of the addresses, and because the most perfect people in love and sincerity are the prophets, especially the Beloved of God (peace be upon him), while obligations are more complete and perfect regarding them, so much so that they are rebuked for the slightest slip, even for leaving the preferable. Yes, it is related about some saint that he asked God to excuse him from obligations and requested release from outward acts of worship, and He answered him by stripping him of reason, which is the basis of obligation; yet he was of high rank as he was. And you are aware that the gnostic does not tire of worship, nor slacken in obedience, nor ask to descend from the peak of perfection to the abyss of deficiency, nor to descend from the stations of the kingdom to the stations of animals; rather, perhaps he attains such complete attraction to the world of holiness and absorption in contemplating the Divine Presence that he departs from this world and neglects obligations without sinning thereby, because he is in the status of one not obligated, like the sleeper, due to his inability to observe both matters and contemplate both sides. So perhaps he asks for permanence in that state and not returning to the world of appearances. This oblivion is the madness that perhaps outweighs some intellects, and those characterized by it are called 'the sane madmen'. And by this the superiority of the prophets over the saints appears: for they, despite their absorption being more complete and their attraction more comprehensive, do not neglect even the slightest act of obedience, nor are they oblivious of this side for an hour, because their holy power is such that nothing distracts them from that Presence, and for this they are blamed for the slightest deviation from the path of rightness.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a nuanced discussion comparing prophethood (nubuwwa) and sainthood (wilaya). The author begins by stating the problem: there is hesitation whether the Prophet's prophethood or his sainthood is superior. Some argue for prophethood because it involves mediation between Heaven and Earth and serving the interests of creation, along with the honor of witnessing the angel. Others lean toward sainthood because it implies a special closeness and exclusivity, which in the Prophet is at its peak. However, the author then reports the view of some mystics that the absolute claim 'sainthood is better than prophethood' is unsound and impolite; it must be qualified: the Prophet's sainthood is better than his prophethood. The reason is that legislative prophethood is tied to a specific time, whereas sainthood (spiritual authority) continues until the Hour. Prophethood in its outward form (informing) ended with Muhammad, but its inward aspect (sainthood) remains, and saints are manifestations of the Prophet's authority, as indicated by their following the Prophet. Next, the author refutes the idea that religious obligations can be dropped for saints. He argues that the prophets are the most perfect in love and sincerity, and obligations are more stringent for them. He dismisses a story about a saint who asked to be excused from obligations and was answered by loss of reason; a true gnostic never tires of worship. The author explains that some saints may become so absorbed in the Divine that they neglect obligations unintentionally, like a sleeper, but this is a deficiency, not perfection. This shows the superiority of prophets: they never neglect any duty despite their higher spiritual state. Their holy power is so complete that nothing distracts them, and they are held accountable for the slightest misstep.

Key Terms
النبوة
الولاية
الوساطة
القرب
الإختصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which opinion argues that prophethood is superior because of mediation?
A) The first opinion
B) The second opinion
C) Both opinions
D) Neither opinion

Key Takeaway
The debate between prophethood and sainthood hinges on different aspects: mediation vs. closeness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your relationship with the Prophet ﷺ, do you find yourself drawn more to his role as the one who brought divine guidance (prophethood) or to his personal closeness to Allah (sainthood)? Which one do you need to nurture more in your daily life?
?
The passage presents two competing aspects of the Prophet’s station. Is there an area in your own spiritual life where you prioritize one dimension of faith (e.g., actions or knowledge) over another? Which one are you neglecting, and what concrete step will you take this week to restore balance?
?
If you truly believed that the Prophet’s sainthood is ‘in utmost perfection’ and that you are far from that, how would it change the way you seek closeness to Allah? Would it increase your hope or your humility? Write down one specific prayer you will say tonight asking for a share of that closeness.

The Qualified View: Prophet's Sainthood Better
Author presents qualified view on sainthood superiority from mystics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why some mystics qualify the claim that sainthood is better, and how prophethood's outward and inward aspects are distinguished.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sainthood is superior to his prophethood because it is everlasting.

The author now presents a more nuanced position from the mystics: the absolute claim 'sainthood is better than prophethood' is incorrect and impolite. Instead, it must be qualified: the Prophet's sainthood is better than his prophethood. This lesson explores the reasoning behind that qualification, especially the distinction between prophethood's outward form (temporary) and inward essence (permanent).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the qualified view
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the key phrase 'لا بد من التقييد' and the reasoning that follows.
The author cites the speech of 'some mystics' (بعض العرفاء).
2
Understand the qualification
Identify what is being qualified: sainthood in general vs. the Prophet's sainthood. The qualification makes the claim acceptable.
3
Grasp the temporal vs. permanent distinction
The author explains that legislative prophethood is tied to a specific time, whereas sainthood continues until the Hour. Prophethood's outward aspect (informing) ended with Muhammad, but its inward aspect (sainthood) remains.
This is why the Prophet's sainthood is considered better—it is ongoing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو يقع تردد في أن نبوة النبي أفضل أم ولايته. فمن قائل بالأول لما في النبوة من معنى الوساطة بين الجانبين والقيام بمصالح الخلق في الدارين، مع شرف مشاهدة الملك. ومن مائل إلى الثاني لما في الولاية من معنى القرب والاختصاص الذي يكون في النبي في غاية الكمال، بخلاف ولاية غير النبي. وفي كلام بعض العرفاء أن ما قيل الولاية أفضل من النبوة لا يصح مطلقاً، وليس من الأدب إطلاق القول به، بل لا بد من التقييد، وهو أن ولاية النبي أفضل من نبوته، لأن نبوة التشريع متعلقة بمصلحة الوقت والولاية لا تعلق لها بوقت دون وقت، بل قام سلطانها إلى قيام الساعة، بخلاف النبوة فإنها مختومة بمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم من حيث ظاهرها الذي هو الإنباء، وإن كانت دائمة من حيث باطنها الذي هو الولاية، أعني التصرف في الخلق بالحق، فإن الأولياء من أمة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم تصرف ولايته بهم، يتصرف في الخلق بالحق إلى قيام الساعة، ولهذا كانت علامتهم المتابعة. إذ ليس الولي إلا مظهر تصرف النبي. وأما بطلان القول بسقوط الأمر والنهي فلعموم الخطابات، ولأن أكمل الناس في المحبة والإخلاص هم الأنبياء، سيما حبيب الله، مع أن التكاليف في حقهم أتم وأكمل، حتى يعاتبون بأدنى زلة، بل بترك الأفضل. نعم حكي عن بعض الأولياء أنه استعفى الله عن التكاليف، وسأله الإعتاق عن ظواهر العبادات، فأجابه إلى ذلك بأن سلبه العقل الذي هو مناط التكليف، ومع ذلك كان من علو المرتبة على ما كان. وأنت خبير بأن العارف لا يسأم من العبادة، ولا يفتر في الطاعة ولا يسأل الهبوط من أوج الكمال إلى حضيض النقصان، والنزول من معارج الملك إلى منازل الحيوان، بل ربما يحصل له كمال الانجذاب إلى عالم القدس والاستغراق في ملاحظة جناب الحق، بحيث يذهب عن هذا العالم، ويخل بالتكاليف من غير تأثم بذلك لكونه في حكم غير المكلف كالنائم، وذلك لعجزه عن مراعاة الأمرين وملاحظة الجانبين، فربما يسأل دوام تلك الحالة، وعدم العود إلى عالم الظاهر، وهذا الذهول هو الجنون الذي ربما يرجح على بعض العقول، والمتسمون به هم المسمون بمجانين العقلاء. وبهذا يظهر فضل الأنبياء على الأولياء، فإنهم مع أن استغراقهم أكمل، وانجذابهم أشمل لا يخلون بأدنى طاعة، ولا يذهلون من هذا الجانب ساعة، لأن قوتهم القدسية من الكمال بحيث لا يشغلها شاغل عن ذلك الجناب، ولهذا ينعى عليهم أدنى زلة عن منهج الصواب.
There occurs hesitation whether the Prophet's prophethood is better or his sainthood. Some say the first because in prophethood there is the meaning of mediation between the two sides and undertaking the interests of creation in both abodes, along with the honor of witnessing the angel. Some incline to the second because in sainthood there is the meaning of proximity and specification which exists in the Prophet in utmost perfection, unlike the sainthood of other than the Prophet. In the speech of some mystics that what was said 'sainthood is better than prophethood' is not absolutely correct, and it is not of proper etiquette to utter it absolutely, rather it must be qualified: that the Prophet's sainthood is better than his prophethood, because legislative prophethood is connected to the benefit of the time, while sainthood has no connection to one time over another; rather its authority stands until the Hour, unlike prophethood, for it is sealed with Muhammad (peace be upon him) in terms of its outward aspect which is conveying news, even if it is permanent in terms of its inward aspect which is sainthood, namely acting upon creation with truth. For the saints of the nation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) manifest his authority through them; he acts upon creation with truth until the Hour, and therefore their mark is [the Prophet's] following. For the saint is nothing but a manifestation of the Prophet's action. As for the invalidity of the saying that commands and prohibitions are dropped, it is due to the generality of the addresses, and because the most perfect people in love and sincerity are the prophets, especially the Beloved of God (peace be upon him), while obligations are more complete and perfect regarding them, so much so that they are rebuked for the slightest slip, even for leaving the preferable. Yes, it is related about some saint that he asked God to excuse him from obligations and requested release from outward acts of worship, and He answered him by stripping him of reason, which is the basis of obligation; yet he was of high rank as he was. And you are aware that the gnostic does not tire of worship, nor slacken in obedience, nor ask to descend from the peak of perfection to the abyss of deficiency, nor to descend from the stations of the kingdom to the stations of animals; rather, perhaps he attains such complete attraction to the world of holiness and absorption in contemplating the Divine Presence that he departs from this world and neglects obligations without sinning thereby, because he is in the status of one not obligated, like the sleeper, due to his inability to observe both matters and contemplate both sides. So perhaps he asks for permanence in that state and not returning to the world of appearances. This oblivion is the madness that perhaps outweighs some intellects, and those characterized by it are called 'the sane madmen'. And by this the superiority of the prophets over the saints appears: for they, despite their absorption being more complete and their attraction more comprehensive, do not neglect even the slightest act of obedience, nor are they oblivious of this side for an hour, because their holy power is such that nothing distracts them from that Presence, and for this they are blamed for the slightest deviation from the path of rightness.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a nuanced discussion comparing prophethood (nubuwwa) and sainthood (wilaya). The author begins by stating the problem: there is hesitation whether the Prophet's prophethood or his sainthood is superior. Their holy power is so complete that nothing distracts them, and they are held accountable for the slightest misstep.

Correction: The absolute claim is incorrect; only the Prophet's sainthood is superior to his prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Prophet's sainthood considered better than his prophethood?
A) Because prophethood involves hardship
B) Because it is permanent and not limited to a time
C) Because saints are higher than prophets
D) Because prophethood ended with Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sainthood surpasses his prophethood in permanence, but the absolute claim that any sainthood is better is unsound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you honestly feel the Prophet's authority alive in your life today, or do you treat his message as a finished historical event? What would change if you truly believed he still acts through those who follow him?
?
When you hear 'sainthood is better than prophethood,' does your heart secretly lean to the false absolute? Can you humbly accept the qualified view, and how might that reshape your reverence for the Prophet?
?
The mark of the saint is following the Prophet (mutaba'a). Search your soul: is your following real and consistent, or just a label? Commit to one concrete act of mutaba'a today—what will it be?

Refuting Exemption and Proving Prophetic Superiority
Author refutes exemption from obligations and proves prophets' superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets cannot be exempt from obligations, and how their perfect state shows their superiority over saints.

Core Idea
Prophets never neglect duties even in the highest spiritual states, proving their superiority.

After discussing the relative merits of prophethood and sainthood, the author addresses a dangerous misconception: that saints (or even prophets) might be exempt from religious obligations. Using arguments from generality of addresses and the prophets' example, he refutes this. He also recounts a story of a saint who asked for exemption and lost his reason, contrasting it with the true gnostic who never tires of worship. Finally, he concludes that prophets are superior because they combine perfect absorption with unwavering fulfillment of duties.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of dropping obligations
Read the section starting from 'وأما بطلان القول بسقوط الأمر والنهي'. Note the two arguments: generality of addresses and the prophets' own example.
2
Understand the story of the saint
The author recounts a saint who asked to be excused from obligations and was stripped of reason. Consider why this is not a desirable state.
The author then describes the true gnostic who never tires.
3
See the final proof of prophetic superiority
The author concludes that prophets, despite their greater absorption, never neglect any act of obedience, unlike some saints who may become oblivious. This shows their perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?
When you experience moments of spiritual closeness or emotional uplift in worship, do you ever feel that the routine of daily obligations becomes burdensome? If the prophets, despite their perfect absorption, were rebuked for leaving the preferable (tark al-afdal), what does that say about your own standards of obedience? Are you content with just the minimum, or do you aspire to follow the Prophet in seeking excellence in every act? What is one 'preferable' act you have been neglecting that you can start doing from today?

Three Objections Against Annihilation and Their Refutations
The author presents three objections to annihilation and provides answers to each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three key objections raised against the doctrine of annihilation and the theological responses provided to each.

Core Idea
Annihilation serves divine purposes beyond human comprehension, refuting objections of injustice or purposelessness.

In this passage, the author addresses three key objections from those who deny that bodies can be annihilated before resurrection. The first objection questions the identity of the resurrected body, the second from the Mu'tazila challenges the purpose of annihilation, and the third appeals to Quranic verses describing revival. The author provides concise answers to each, reinforcing the possibility of annihilation as part of God's plan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three objections
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Then read the translation. Notice that the passage is structured as three objections followed by answers. Highlight each objection and its corresponding answer.
2
Examine the first objection and its dismissal
The first objection claims that if the resurrected body is not identical to the original, recompense would not reach the same person. Note how the author dismisses this by referring to a prior discussion – it is considered weak.
This shows reliance on previously established arguments.
3
Analyze the second objection and its thorough answer
The Mu'tazilite objection states that annihilation has no purpose and cannot serve as just recompense. The answer lists several purposes: kindness to the believer, manifesting divine majesty and independence, and demonstrating God's unique permanence.
This refutation uses theological purposes rather than philosophical arguments.
4
Understand the third objection and its counterargument
The third objection cites Quranic verses that describe resurrection as reviving after death, implying no annihilation. The author responds by noting these verses focus on revival, not on the state before revival, and are countered by other verses alluding to annihilation.
This shows how Quranic interpretation must consider the context and other verses.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how each objection is answered: the first is dismissed as weak, the second is countered with positive purposes, and the third is shown not to preclude annihilation. The passage strengthens the case for annihilation as possible and purposeful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: احتج الآخرون . احتج الآخرون بوجوه : الأول ـ أن المعاد بعد العدم ليس هو المبتدأ بعينه، فلا يكون الجزاء واصلاً . إلى مستحقه، وقد عرفت ضعفه . الثاني - وهو المعتزلة، أنه لا يتصور في الإعدام غرض، إذ لا منفعة فيه لأحد، ولا يصلح جزاء الفعل. وأجيب بأن من الغرض اللطف للمكلف، وإظهار العظمة والاستغناء، والتفرد بالدوام والبقاء. الثالث - الآيات المشعرة بأن النشور بالإحياء بعد الموت، والجمع بعد التفرق: أرني كيف تحيي الموتى (٢) وأنى يُحيي هذه الله بعد موتها (٣) وكذلك النشور (٤) وكذلك تخرجون (٥) إلى غير ذك والجواب - ان غايتها عدم الدلالة على الإعدام لكونها مسوقة لبيان الإحياء والجمع . ثم هي معارضة بآيات تشعر بالفناء كما سبق .
He said: The others argued. The others argued with aspects: First, that the returned being after non-existence is not the same as the first being, so the recompense would not reach its deserved one, and you have known its weakness. Second, and it is the Mu'tazila: that no purpose can be conceived in annihilation, since there is no benefit in it for anyone, nor is it suitable as a recompense for an action. And it was answered: that among the purposes are kindness to the morally responsible (al-mukallaf), manifesting majesty and independence, and uniqueness in perpetuity and permanence. Third, the verses indicating that resurrection is by reviving after death and gathering after dispersion: 'Show me how you give life to the dead' (2:260), 'How does Allah give life to this after its death?' (2:259), and likewise 'resurrection' (35:9), and 'thus you will be brought forth' (30:19), and others. And the answer: that their ultimate import is that they do not indicate annihilation because they are presented to explain revival and gathering; moreover, they are contradicted by verses that indicate annihilation as mentioned before.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage presents three objections raised by opponents against the doctrine of annihilation, likely from those who deny bodily resurrection after complete non-existence. The first objection: if the resurrected body is not identical to the original, the reward or punishment would not reach the same person. The author dismisses this as weak, referencing earlier discussion. The second objection, attributed to the Mu'tazila: there is no purpose in annihilation since it benefits no one and cannot serve as a just recompense. The answer: annihilation can serve purposes such as showing kindness to the believer (lutf), manifesting divine majesty and independence, and demonstrating God's unique permanence. The third objection: many Quranic verses describe resurrection as reviving after death and gathering after dispersion, implying the body is not annihilated but dispersed. The author responds: these verses are not about annihilation; they focus on revival and gathering. Furthermore, they are countered by other verses alluding to annihilation (as discussed earlier). Thus, the objections fail to disprove annihilation.

Key Terms
المعاد
المبتدأ
الجزاء
اللطف
النشور
الإحياء
الجمع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think annihilation contradicts divine justice because the resurrected person might not be the same individual.
Correction: The passage shows that the identity objection is weak (previously refuted), and annihilation can serve divinely ordained purposes like kindness and manifesting majesty.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the Mu'tazilite objection that there is no purpose in annihilation?
A) He agrees and says annihilation is purposeless.
B) He says annihilation serves purposes like kindness to the believer and manifesting divine attributes.
C) He denies the objection entirely by saying annihilation is the only possible outcome.
D) He argues that the Mu'tazila have already been refuted elsewhere.

Key Takeaway
The three objections against annihilation—identity, purposelessness, and scriptural evidence—are all refuted by reasoned theological responses, defending the possibility and purposefulness of annihilation in divine plan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that annihilation serves purposes like kindness and manifesting divine majesty. Think of a time when you lost something important—perhaps a relationship, a job, or your health. Did you see that loss as entirely purposeless? How might reframing it as an act of divine kindness or a demonstration of God’s majesty change your heart toward that experience? Are you willing to thank God for the purging, even if it hurt?
?
The Mu'tazila objected that annihilation has no benefit for anyone. Reflect on your own attachments: what are you clinging to that you assume will last forever? How does the realization that God alone is truly permanent challenge your sense of security in temporary things? What would it look like to release your grip on something you fear losing, trusting that even if it is annihilated, God has a purpose?
?
The first objection worried that if the resurrected body isn't the same as the original, then justice wouldn't be served. Have you ever felt that God's justice could not reach you because you felt scattered or changed beyond recognition? The passage affirms that despite annihilation, justice is possible. In what area of your life do you doubt that God can 'gather' your fragmented self and hold you accountable as the same person? Will you surrender that doubt to the truth that He is able to restore and recompense?

Neutral Souls and Their Afterlife: Transmigration or Celestial Attachment?
Discusses neutral souls and philosophers' views on their post-mortem state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic theological concept of neutral souls and the philosophical proposals for their post-mortem state, including transmigration and attachment to celestial bodies.

Core Idea
Neutral souls escape punishment but philosophers debate how they continue to perceive after death.

This passage from the Maqasid discusses a category of souls that are neither perfect nor wicked—they are 'sound' (salima) but lack perfection. After death, they are granted a happiness befitting them, untouched by suffering. However, some philosophers found it impossible for such souls to remain inactive in perception, leading to theories about their continued existence. The text presents two main philosophical views: transmigration and the attachment to celestial bodies advocated by Ibn Sina and al-Farabi.

Guided Path
1
Understand the description of neutral souls
Read the first part describing souls free from perfection, its opposite, and desire for perfection. They remain in God's mercy and experience a happiness suited to them, not suffering.
This is the baseline: neutral souls are not punished.
2
Note the philosophers' objection
Some philosophers argued that such souls cannot be completely inactive with respect to perception, because perception requires bodily instruments.
This premise drives the need for a post-mortem attachment.
3
Identify the two possibilities
The passage says: either they become souls of other bodies (transmigration) or they attach without becoming souls. Find these two options in the text.
Transmigration is explicitly named as 'tanasukh'.
4
Examine the view of Ibn Sina and al-Farabi
They chose the second option: souls attach to celestial bodies not as managers but as instruments for imagination, allowing them to imagine forms and behold otherworldly goods.
This is a philosophical attempt to explain continued perception without reincarnation.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this differs from the Islamic doctrine of bodily resurrection. Why might philosophers prefer celestial attachment over transmigration?
This connects to broader theological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النفوس السليمة الخالية عن الكمال، وعما يضاده، وعن الشوق الى الكمال، فتبقى في سعة من رحمة الله تعالى ، خالصة من البدن إلى سعادة تليق بها غير متألمة بما يتأذى به الأشقياء، إلا أنه ذهب بعض الفلاسفة إلى أنها لا يجوز أن تكون معطلة عن الإدراك، فلا بد أن تتعلق بأجسام أخر لما أنها لا تدرك إلا بالآلات الجسمانية، وحينئذ إما أن تصير مبادىء صور لها، وتكون نفوساً لها، وهذا هو القول بالتناسخ، وإما أن لا تصير، وهذا هو الذي مال إليه ابن سينا (۳) والفارابي (٤) من أنها تتعلق بأجرام سماوية، لا على أن تكون نفوساً لها مدبرة لأمورها، بل على أن تستعملها لإمكان التخيل، ثم تتخيل الصور التي كانت معتدة عندها وفي وهمها، فتشاهد الخيرات الأخروية على حسب ما تتخيلها .
As for the sound souls that are free from perfection, from what opposes it, and from desire for perfection, they remain in the expanse of God's mercy, purified from the body to a happiness befitting them, not pained by what the wretched suffer. However, some philosophers held that they cannot be inactive with respect to perception, so they must attach to other bodies because they do not perceive except through bodily instruments. Then either they become principles of forms for them and become souls for them — this is the doctrine of transmigration (tanasukh) — or they do not become so. This latter is what Ibn Sina and al-Farabi inclined to: that they attach to celestial bodies, not as souls managing their affairs, but using them for the possibility of imagination, then they imagine the forms that were present with them and in their fancy, and so they behold the otherworldly goods according to how they imagine them.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage addresses souls that are 'sound' (سليمة) — lacking both perfection and its opposite, and lacking even the desire for perfection. They are not punished; they remain in God's mercy and experience a happiness suited to them, untouched by the suffering of the wretched. The passage then notes a view of some philosophers (some of the falasifa) who argued that such souls cannot be completely without perception (معطلة عن الإدراك). Since perception requires bodily instruments, these souls must attach to other bodies. This leads to two possibilities: either they become the souls of those bodies (i.e., transmigration or تناسخ), or they attach without becoming the soul. Ibn Sina and al-Farabi took the latter view: the soul attaches to celestial bodies (أجرام سماوية) not as a managing soul, but as a means for imagination, allowing it to imagine forms it was familiar with, and thus behold the goods of the afterlife as imagined.

Key Terms
نَفْس سَلِيمَة (sound soul)
تَنَاسُخ (transmigration)
أَجْرَام سَمَاوِيَّة (celestial bodies)
تَخَيُّل (imagination)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All souls that are not perfect are punished in the afterlife.
Correction: The passage teaches that sound souls (neutral) are not punished; they remain in God's mercy and experience a happiness befitting them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do Ibn Sina and al-Farabi believe happens to neutral souls after death?
A) They cease to exist
B) They transmigrate into new bodies on earth
C) They attach to celestial bodies to engage in imagination
D) They remain completely inactive

Key Takeaway
Sound souls avoid punishment, but philosophers differ on how they continue to perceive: either by transmigration or by using celestial bodies for imagination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson describes souls that lack even the desire for perfection. Examine your own heart: do you truly long for spiritual perfection, or have you become complacent? What one habit can you change today to stir that desire?
?
The neutral souls are not pained by the suffering of the wretched. Are there people suffering around you whom you have learned to ignore? Ask Allah to soften your heart and commit to one concrete act of empathy this week.
?
The philosophers argued that the soul's imagination after death is shaped by the forms it held in life. What are you filling your mind with right now—through media, conversations, and thoughts—that will form your spiritual imagination in the Hereafter? Will you make a deliberate change today to feed your soul with images of khayr?
